< review>
After reading so many good reviews, we were very excited to work with Jerry's.  However... we were only disappointed with the service we received.

My wife took her dress in to get it altered prior to a military ball.  When we went to pick up (on the date we were told to), they could not find the dress.  When they found it, the alterations were not complete.  Because of this, she had to scramble to find a dress to wear to the ball!

When my wife went back (over a month later...Why hurry when they already failed to meet their promised timeline?), the dress still did not fit her well and the beading had been damaged.  On top of that, Jerry would not accept the fact that the dress was poorly altered to fit her.  I called the shop later, and Jerry was equally as rude to me.

Jerry's may be decent with uniforms, but there are too many great tailors in the area to risk wasting your money on dress alterations here.  I now have to pay someone else to do the job that Jerry's promised they could do initially.< /review>

< Text>
Received the worst customer service I've ever had in my entire life here. After one of the washing machines finished, I tried to open the door, but some kind of error code came up on its display, and wouldn't open. I told one of the associates about it, and she blamed it on me saying it was because I tried to open it before the cycle finished. She then left to grab some tools, but very loudly and obviously huffed and puffed saying "WHY OH WHY" so that everyone nearby could hear.

She came back to the machine with a screw driver, with no luck, and I explained to her that she can check her cameras to see if I tried to open the door before the cycle finished. She still gave me attitude afterwards, and went to her cashier desk to call her family (I think) to ask for some extra tools. She got frustrated and actually yelled into the phone, with what I think were Spaniah expletives - again, so that everyone can hear and try and make me feel bad.

Afterward, I checked one of the other machines I used, and I saw that that door was locked, too. I told her about that, and she loudly said "I WONDER WHY". We walked back to the first machine that had problems, and I told her I did not appreciate her attitude toward me in front of all the customers. From there on she kept yelling, but at that point I just ignored her ignorant self and stopped paying attention to what she was saying.

I'd like to believe this was racially motivated, but I won't say for certain. All I know is that I was the only Asian customer there, and after our argument, she started talking to the other Latinos standing nearby in Spanish, very obviously about me.

Incredibly rude, and overall trashy behavior. Even if I did make the mistake of trying to open the doors before the cycle finished (who would even do that anyway?), the associate's response was way out of line. I will never be a customer at this place again.<//Text>

< Review>
I never thought I would go out of my way to write a negative review about a restaurant, but I feel that my experience at this place has to be written about somewhere. I did visit for my first time here on Valentine's Day, so given the hectic nature of this "holiday" at restaurants, perhaps I just chose the wrong first day. Anyway, the dinner for two included an appetizer, main meal and dessert, all bundled up to $60 per person. This was more than I have ever paid at a dinner for two at even more "luxurious" locations in LA, but given the date, I still attended expecting to be blown away.
The Appetizer: A small plate with cured beef surrounding a thin salad. The beef was thin yet flavorful, but unknowingly ordering a new type of food with a strange name resulted in being intimidated by uncooked beef, so I didn't really enjoy it too much. Given it was my fault, I continued onto the main dish.
The Main Meal: I don't think I have ever tasted a more dry, flavorless chicken at a restaurant. The flavor matched the kind I make at home on a George Foreman grill when I'm in a hurry. Given that this was to be the main meal of the evening, the portion size was a terrible disappointment as well. It was simply a breaded piece of chicken breast coated with yet another thin layer of salad and a couple of tomato pieces scattered throughout the dish. No sides or anything, just plain chicken and uncomfortably thin greenery.
Dessert: Best part of meal, 3 scoops of assorted sorbet in a small plate.
The $4 tea I was served only lasted me 1 small ~6 oz. cup, since it was removed after the appetizer and never returned after that. The tea was nothing extraordinary, only a selection of assorted tea bags one could find at a Rite Aid or CVS. The Valet gentleman tipped over my girlfriend's roses when retrieving the car, and spilled water all over her laptop bag. Given the poor service, overcrowded environment and small portions of food for such a high price, I decided not to leave a tip, as I was on somewhat of a budget. Now, I have always been a courteous tipper, leaving the average amount and often more when service is great, but this time I just couldn't bring myself around to do it. Regardless, the restaurant decided to charge the 18% gratuity fee onto my card although I specifically signed a different total on the receipt. I was notified that my checking account was over-drafted this morning by a couple of bucks because of this. I guess I learned my lesson, dinner on Valentine's Day is the worst idea ever. I will attempt to call and get the money refunded, given that as far as I was concerned, a gratuity fee was not mandatory, especially for only a party of two.</Review>
